--- Commit Message ---
LU-18813 osd-wbcfs: MemFS-based OSD with writeback support

Implement a memory filesystem based OSD with writeback support for
Lustre.
It borrows lots of design from memory-based file systems such as
tmpfs/ramfs. The data is first written into the memory-based file
system (called MemFS for short). And then, the data can be flushed
to the persistent storage in a delayed write-back manner.

This patch implemented the basic functionality to store data in
MemFS. It can reuse lots of VFS codes in Linux kernel such as:
- Page caching for data;
- dcache for dentry management and lookup;
- icache for inode management and lookup;
- Writeback mechanism in Linux kernel

--- Message (Timothy Day, 2025-03-18 05:49:03.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

(5 comments)

Ran a couple tests:

1) llog_test.ko on a stand-alone MGS: This passes and seems to work well. Although I do see a 
"VFS: Busy inodes after unmount of wbcfs" warning after umount.

2) I see some DEBUG_RWSEMS_WARN_ON(sem->magic != sem) errors on server mount when running on a debug kernel. I can't tell which semaphore this is. Something in local_oid_storage_init() complaining.

3) Ran sanity.sh: I consistently hit the iput() crash (mentioned below) on sanity/15. The other tests (before that one) seem to pass.

4) git-clone/compilation/build: I can clone a git repo just fine. But after a client umount/mount, the directories remain the the block data seems to disappear. I don't know why this fails but the llog tests work.

The fourth issue is the biggest one stopping me from trying more tests.

One other thought: I think the debugging infrastructure is more comprehensive in OSD-mem. It's easier (IMO) to track the object lifecycle because there's more instrumentation on each function.

 echo 3 > /proc/sys/vm/drop_caches

all of the data in the OSD gets flushed. Somewhere on the write path, I think we need to explicitly dirty all of the pages that have data.

--- Message (Timothy Day, 2025-05-13 03:17:30.000000000) ---
Patch Set 32:

Seems like we are missing a symbol on CentOS 7. We'd need to define this:

/*
 * Retaining negative dentries for an in-memory filesystem just wastes
 * memory and lookup time: arrange for them to be deleted immediately.
 */
int always_delete_dentry(const struct dentry *dentry)
{
	return 1;
}
EXPORT_SYMBOL(always_delete_dentry);

const struct dentry_operations simple_dentry_operations = {
	.d_delete = always_delete_dentry,
};
EXPORT_SYMBOL(simple_dentry_operations);

IMHO, I think Janitor testing for the OSD should start on RHEL8 if you're moving to that soon anyway.

--- Message (Oleg Drokin, 2025-05-13 04:50:55.000000000) ---
Patch Set 32:

(15 comments)

I propose to rip out all the pre-4.18 compat bits. I understand that it was mostly done to support centos7 that we really hope to deprecate even in th bowels of janitor test relatively soon.
As such cannot really justify a lot of that cruft and the time wasted on it going forward, esp since we get no value out of it as it still does not even insert thanks to some missing kernel export symbols.
So can we just replace all that with a simple test for something that if not present would entirely disable wbcfs building whatsoever?
We still would get the (quick) build-test out of janitor because it builds on rhel8.x and smatch is also rocky8.10 based.
